## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator problem where acceleration depends on position, velocity, and possibly time. The nonlinearity can appear in restoring forces (Duffing-type), damping (van der Pol-type), or through parametric/external driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinearity)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 + c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Van der Pol form: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (expanded nonlinear damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-dependent stiffness)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity damping)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v + c4 * cos(c5 * t)
- Softening spring with drive: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (quadratic nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium → symmetric potential wells
- Even-power position terms (x²) break spatial symmetry → asymmetric oscillation / Helmholtz-type behavior
- Velocity-position coupling terms like x²·v indicate amplitude-dependent damping (van der Pol mechanism)
- Trigonometric functions of time (sin/cos of c·t) indicate external periodic driving forces
- Negative linear damping (positive coefficient on v) combined with cubic terms (x²·v) produces self-sustained limit cycles
- Cubic position terms with opposite sign to linear term (c0·x - c1·x³ with same-sign c0,c1) indicate double-well (bistable) potential
- Products of time-periodic functions with position (cos(c·t)·x) indicate parametric resonance mechanisms
- Odd velocity powers (v³) represent symmetric nonlinear drag forces analogous to turbulent damping

GT Equivalence Verification (PO20)
============================================================
GT: -alpha*v**c0 - beta*log(Abs(v) + c1) - c2*beta*v - mu*(c3 - v**c4)*v - omega0**c5*(gamma*Abs(v)**c6 + c7)*x
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to analyze whether any candidate formula can match the Ground Truth (GT).

**GT numerical expression:**
`-0.0441723*v³ - 0.333481*v*(1 - v²) - 1.24947*v - 3.58221*x*(0.047928*|v|^(1/3) + 1) - 0.624737*log(|v| + 1)`

Let me expand this:
- `-0.0441723*v³`
- `-0.333481*v + 0.333481*v³`
- `-1.24947*v`
- `-3.58221*x*0.047928*|v|^(1/3) - 3.58221*x`
- `-0.624737*log(|v| + 1)`

Combining terms:
- **v³**: (-0.0441723 + 0.333481) = 0.289309*v³
- **v**: (-0.333481 - 1.24947) = -1.58295*v
- **x**: -3.58221*x
- **x·|v|^(1/3)**: -0.17166*x*|v|^(1/3)
- **log(|v|+1)**: -0.624737*log(|v|+1)

So GT = c_a*x + c_b*v + c_c*v³ + c_d*x*|v|^(1/3) + c_e*log(|v|+1)

Key structural features of GT:
1. Linear in x
2. Linear in v
3. Cubic in v (v³)
4. Term: x·|v|^(1/3) — this couples x and v with a fractional power of |v|
5. log(|v|+1) — logarithm of |v|+1
6. **No dependence on t at all**

Since GT has no t-dependence, any candidate with t-dependent terms must be able to zero them out.

The GT has a `log(|v|+1)` term and an `x*|v|^(1/3)` term. Let me look for candidates that can produce both.

**Candidate 40**: `c0*x + c1*v + c2*v³ + c3*v^c4 + c5*log(c6*v+1) + c7*v*(c8+t)² + c9*t*v²`

For t-independence: The term `c7*v*(c8+t)²` expands to `c7*v*c8² + 2*c7*v*c8*t + c7*v*t²`. Combined with `c9*t*v²`, we need `c7=0` (to kill t-dependent terms) and `c9=0`. Then we get: `c0*x + c1*v + c2*v³ + c3*v^c4 + c5*log(c6*v+1)`. This has `log(c6*v+1)` not `log(|v|+1)`, and no `x*|v|^(1/3)` term. **No match.**

The critical term is `x*|v|^(1/3)`. I need a candidate that has a term coupling x with a power of v (or |v|).

**Candidate 30**: `c0*x + c1*v + c2*v³ + c3*v^c4 + c5*v^c6 + c7*x*(c8+v)^c9`

The term `c7*x*(c8+v)^c9`: if c8=0, this becomes `c7*x*v^c9`. Setting c9=1/3 gives `c7*x*v^(1/3)`. But GT has `|v|^(1/3)`, not `v^(1/3)`. For v>0 these match but not for v<0. Also, there's no log term here. **No match.**

Looking for `log(|v|+1)` or equivalent: Most candidates have `log(c*t+1)` or `log(c*x+1)` or `log(c*v+1)`, not `log(|v|+1)`.

None of the candidates have both:
- A `log(|v|+1)` term (or equivalent)
- An `x*|v|^(1/3)` term (or equivalent)

The GT requires both these structural elements, and no candidate provides both. Most candidates don't even have a log term involving v, and the x*|v|^(1/3) coupling is absent from nearly all.

After careful analysis of all 50 candidates, none can reproduce the GT's structure which requires simultaneously: `log(|v|+1)`, `x·|v|^(1/3)`, `v`, `v³`, and `x` terms with no t-dependence.

Let me expand this:
- `-0.0441723*v³`
- `-0.333481*v + 0.333481*v³`
- `-1.24947*v`
- `-3.58221*x*0.047928*|v|^(1/3) - 3.58221*x`
- `-0.624737*log(|v| + 1)`

Combining terms:
- **v³**: (-0.0441723 + 0.333481) = 0.289309*v³
- **v**: (-0.333481 - 1.24947) = -1.58295*v
- **x**: -3.58221*x
- **x·|v|^(1/3)**: -0.17168*x*|v|^(1/3)
- **log(|v|+1)**: -0.624737*log(|v|+1)

So GT = c_a*x + c_b*v + c_c*v³ + c_d*x*|v|^(1/3) + c_e*log(|v|+1)

The GT has these basis functions: **x, v, v³, x·|v|^(1/3), log(|v|+1)**

Key observations:
- GT has **no dependence on t**
- GT has **x·|v|^(1/3)** term (not just x)
- GT has **log(|v|+1)** term
- GT has **no v² term** (standalone)
- GT has **no v·x² term**
- GT has **no exponential terms**

Now let me check each candidate. For a candidate to match, it must be able to reproduce exactly these 5 basis functions with no extra terms that can't be zeroed out.

For candidates with `t`-dependent terms: these can only match if all `t`-dependent coefficients can be set to zero.

For candidates with `v**c4` type terms: `|v|^(1/3)` alone doesn't appear in GT, but `x*|v|^(1/3)` does. A standalone `v**c4` term cannot produce `x*|v|^(1/3)`.

**Critical check**: The GT requires `x*|v|^(1/3)` and `log(|v|+1)`. Let me check which candidates have both.

Looking through all candidates, none have an `x*|v|^c` term combined with `log(|v|+1)`. Most candidates have `v**c4` (standalone power of v, not multiplied by x) and lack `log(|v|+1)`.

The GT needs `x*|v|^(1/3)` which requires a term like `x*|v|^c` or `x*(something with v)`. Looking at candidates with `x*(...)^c` terms: Candidates 25, 27, 30, 31, 37, 41, 48 have terms like `x*(c8+v)**c9` but these expand differently from `x*|v|^(1/3)`.

Candidate 30: `c0*x + c1*v + c2*v³ + c3*v^c4 + c5*v^c6 + c7*x*(c8+v)^c9`
- The term `c7*x*(c8+v)^c9` with c8=0, c9=1/3 gives `c7*x*v^(1/3)`, but this isn't `x*|v|^(1/3)` since v can be negative. Also needs `log(|v|+1)` which is missing.

None of the candidates contain `log(|v|+1)` or `log(Abs(v)+1)` as a term. Candidate 40 has `log(c6*v+1)` which is NOT the same as `log(|v|+1)`.

Since the GT requires `log(|v|+1)` and `x*|v|^(1/3)` as essential basis functions, and no candidate provides both (or even `log(|v|+1)`), none can match.
